</table>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Um_Azzenar_Church.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Um_Azzenar_Church.jpg/220px-Um_Azzenar_Church.jpg" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Um_Azzenar_Church.jpg/330px-Um_Azzenar_Church.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Um_Azzenar_Church.jpg/440px-Um_Azzenar_Church.jpg 2x" data-file-width="720" data-file-height="960" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Um_Azzenar_Church.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Saint Mary Church of the Holy Girdle is a historical Syriac Orthodox Church in Homs, Syria. The church is built over an underground church dating back to 50 AD. It is the seat of the Syriac Orthodox archbishopric. Homs is famous for its black stones and rocks of which this church and many others were built. Photo: Daniel Demeter founder of Syria Photo Guide.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Homs was one of the largest cities in Syria in the 12th century with a population of 7,000.<sup id="cite_ref-Shatzmiller_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shatzmiller-54">[54]</a></sup> In 1785, the inhabitants of Homs numbered more than 2,000 and the population was divided almost evenly between <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church_of_Antioch" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern Orthodox Church of Antioch">Eastern Orthodox Christians</a> and Muslims. The 1860s saw a rise in the population to 15,000–20,000.<sup id="cite_ref-Dumper2_34-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dumper2-34">[34]</a></sup> By 1907, Homs had roughly 65,000 inhabitants, of which two thirds were Muslims and the remainder Christians.<sup id="cite_ref-Cook_14-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cook-14">[14]</a></sup> In the 1981 census, the population stood at 346,871,<sup id="cite_ref-Census_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Census-56">[56]</a></sup> rising to 540,133 in 1994.<sup id="cite_ref-UN_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN-57">[57]</a></sup> According to the 2004 census by Syria's <a href="/wiki/Central_Bureau_of_Statistics_(Syria)" title="Central Bureau of Statistics (Syria)">Central Bureau of Statistics</a>, Homs had a population of 652,609 of which 51.5% were male and 48.5% female.<sup id="cite_ref-CBS_58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CBS-58">[58]</a></sup> In an independent 2005 estimate the city had 750,000 residents,<sup id="cite_ref-Dumper1_10-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dumper1-10">[10]</a></sup> and as of 2008<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Homs&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> the population was estimated at about 823,000.<sup id="cite_ref-Carter2008-2_23-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carter2008-2-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<p>Today, Homs' population reflects Syria's general religious diversity, and is made up primarily of <a href="/wiki/Sunni_Muslim" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunni Muslim">Sunni Muslims</a>, with minorities of <a href="/wiki/Alawites" title="Alawites">Alawite Muslims</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church_of_Antioch" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern Orthodox Church of Antioch">Eastern Orthodox Christians</a> and <a href="/wiki/Syriac_Orthodox_Church" title="Syriac Orthodox Church">Syriac Orthodox Christians</a>. In addition to Catholics, Evangelists and Maronites.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> In the 1880s, the Survey of Western Palestine noted that there were 5,500 Greek Orthodox Christians and 1,500 Syriac Orthodox Christians. The <a href="/wiki/Syriac_Orthodox_Church#Patriarchate_of_Antioch" title="Syriac Orthodox Church">Syriac Patriarchate</a> was transferred to Homs from <a href="/wiki/Mardin" title="Mardin">Mardin</a> in 1933, but relocated once more to Damascus in 1959.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Genocide" title="Armenian Genocide">Armenian Genocide</a> in the early 20th century, about 20,000 <a href="/wiki/Armenians_in_Syria" title="Armenians in Syria">Armenians</a> immigrated to Homs and the surrounding villages.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> A small <a href="/wiki/Greeks_in_Syria" title="Greeks in Syria">Greek</a> community also exists in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-gmfa_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gmfa-64">[64]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Homs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Souq_al-harir_-_Hims,_Syria.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Souq_al-harir_-_Hims%2C_Syria.jpg/170px-Souq_al-harir_-_Hims%2C_Syria.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Souq_al-harir_-_Hims%2C_Syria.jpg/255px-Souq_al-harir_-_Hims%2C_Syria.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Souq_al-harir_-_Hims%2C_Syria.jpg/340px-Souq_al-harir_-_Hims%2C_Syria.jpg 2x" data-file-width="768" data-file-height="1024" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Souq_al-harir_-_Hims,_Syria.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Souk al-Harir, one of the many roofed <i><a href="/wiki/Souk" class="mw-redirect" title="Souk">souks</a></i></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After long periods of stagnation under <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Syria" title="Ottoman Syria">Ottoman</a> rule, Homs started to flourish again in the 20th century. Its geographic and strategic location has made it a centre of agriculture and industry. The "Homs Irrigation Scheme", the first of its kind in modern Syria, brought prosperity to cultivators and the long-established enterprises involved in the processing of agricultural and pastoral products.<sup id="cite_ref-Dumper3_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dumper3-65">[65]</a></sup> Crops grown in Homs include, wheat, barley, lentils, sugar beets, cotton, and vines, as well as serving as a point of exchange between the sedentary zone and the desert. Moreover, because of easy access to the Mediterranean, Homs has attracted overland trade from the <a href="/wiki/Persian_Gulf" title="Persian Gulf">Persian Gulf</a> and <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-commins_41-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-commins-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<p>Homs is also home to several large public heavy industries, such as the oil refinery west of the city which opened in 1959.<sup id="cite_ref-Dumper3_65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dumper3-65">[65]</a></sup> A fertilizer plant was built in 1971 to process phosphates from their deposits near Palmyra; the fertilizer is for domestic consumption and export.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> A growing private industrial sector has flourished in the past decade and many small to medium-sized enterprises occupy the industrial zones northwest and south of the city. A new sugar refinery is being built by a <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazilian</a> company, and an automobile plant is under construction by <a href="/wiki/Iran_Khodro" title="Iran Khodro">Iran Khodro</a>. Also a new phosphate plant and oil refinery are being built east of the city. Homs is also the hub of an important road and rail network, it is the central link between the interior cities and the Mediterranean coast.</p>
<p>A major industrial project was the establishment of a new industrial city in <a href="/wiki/Hisyah" title="Hisyah">Hisyah</a>, 47 kilometers (29&#160;mi) south of the city of Homs. Spreading across some 2,500 hectares (25&#160;km<sup>2</sup>), the city covers four main industrial sectors: textiles, food, chemical, engineering and vocational. In all, the facilities are designed to accommodate up to 66,000 workers and their families. Moreover, a free zone has been established within the city.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<p>The hinterland of Homs is well known for its grapes which are used in Syria's <a href="/wiki/Liqueur" title="Liqueur">liqueur</a> industry, particularly in producing <a href="/wiki/Arak_(drink)" title="Arak (drink)">arak</a>, nectar wine, and <a href="/wiki/Red_wine" title="Red wine">red wine</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> The city is considered a good base for day trips and excursions to the many historical and touristic sights nearby. Popular destinations include <a href="/wiki/Krak_des_Chevaliers" title="Krak des Chevaliers">Krak des Chevaliers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Qatna" title="Qatna">Qatna</a>, <a href="/wiki/Talkalakh" title="Talkalakh">Talkalakh</a> and <a href="/wiki/Marmarita" title="Marmarita">Marmarita</a>. Homs has several hotels; <a href="/wiki/Safir_Hotels_%26_Resorts" title="Safir Hotels &amp; Resorts">Safir Hotel</a> is considered one of Syria's best five-star hotels and the only one of that status in the city. An-Nasr al-Jedid Hotel is built in a 100-year-old mansion and is labeled by tour guides as the "best budget hotel in Homs". Other hotels include Hotel al-Mimas, Ghazi Hotel, and Hotel Khayyam.<sup id="cite_ref-cart158_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cart158-69">[69]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Homs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Homs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Beit_al-Agha_Restaurant_-_Hims,_Syria.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Beit_al-Agha_Restaurant_-_Hims%2C_Syria.jpg/220px-Beit_al-Agha_Restaurant_-_Hims%2C_Syria.jpg" width="220" height="117" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Beit_al-Agha_Restaurant_-_Hims%2C_Syria.jpg/330px-Beit_al-Agha_Restaurant_-_Hims%2C_Syria.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Beit_al-Agha_Restaurant_-_Hims%2C_Syria.jpg/440px-Beit_al-Agha_Restaurant_-_Hims%2C_Syria.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="544" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Beit_al-Agha_Restaurant_-_Hims,_Syria.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Courtyard of Beit al-Agha restaurant</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Although people in Homs eat the same foods common in <a href="/wiki/Levantine_cuisine" title="Levantine cuisine">Levantine cuisine</a>, the city is well known throughout Syria for its own cuisine. A prominent dish is <i>Batarsh</i>, a type of <a href="/wiki/Baba_ghanouj" class="mw-redirect" title="Baba ghanouj">baba ghanouj</a> made with yogurt and garlic instead of <i><a href="/wiki/Tahini" title="Tahini">tahini</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> Homs is also home to a variety of <i>kibbeh mishwiyyeh</i> or "grilled kibbeh". It consists of two pancakes of <i><a href="/wiki/Kibbeh" title="Kibbeh">kibbeh</a></i> stuffed with ground lamb, cooked with lamb fat and various spices.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> <i>Batata mahshi</i> ("stuffed potatoes") is native dish in Homs and is made of baby potatoes stuffed with minced lamb, pine nuts and pomegranate molasses.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> The city specializes in cooking a type of <a href="/wiki/Okra" title="Okra">okra</a> meal, known as <i>bamya bi-l zayt</i> ("okra with olive oil").<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup></p>
<p>Homs has an array of restaurants, some of the most highly acclaimed are those within the Safir Hotel: Mamma Mia and Mersia. The former specializes in <a href="/wiki/Italian_cuisine" title="Italian cuisine">Italian cuisine</a>, while the latter serves <a href="/wiki/Arab_cuisine" title="Arab cuisine">Arabic food</a>. For the local population, popular restaurants include Prince Restaurant which acts as a type of fast-food place, serving <i><a href="/wiki/Shawarma" title="Shawarma">shawarma</a></i>, grilled chicken, and other common Syrian foods, as well as homemade juices. In the Old City, low-price restaurants are grouped together along <a href="/wiki/Quwatli_Street" class="mw-redirect" title="Quwatli Street">Shoukri al-Quwatly Street</a> and sell similar foods, such as <a href="/wiki/Hummus" title="Hummus">hummus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Falafel" title="Falafel">falafel</a>, various salads (<i><a href="/wiki/Mezze" class="mw-redirect" title="Mezze">mezze</a></i>), <a href="/wiki/Shish_kebab" title="Shish kebab">shish kebab</a> and chicken dishes. Restaurants and coffeehouses typically offer <a href="/wiki/Hookah" title="Hookah">hookahs</a> and are a common place for men to gather and smoke.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> Other notable restaurants include Broasted Kreish, a local favorite for <a href="/wiki/Shish_taouk" title="Shish taouk">shish taouk</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shawarma" title="Shawarma">shawarma</a> on the Korniche St just south of the Ghouta; the Rawda, a garden lounge located by the New Clock Tower which is known by locals for its Homsi-style <a href="/wiki/Fatteh" title="Fatteh">fatteh</a> and for the atmosphere created by its divided men and family areas, providing an area for men to gather to play cards, smoke and watch soccer games and for families to have a drink and dessert on late downtime.</p>
<p>Homs also recently emerged as the restaurant scene in pre-civil-war Syria after completing its Malab St. Hamra development. The Hamra Street in the Malab area was home to a strip of highly rated restaurants including La Luna, a <a href="/wiki/Shisha_lounge" class="mw-redirect" title="Shisha lounge">shisha lounge</a>; Chez Moi, serving a few French dishes along with the typical local food; Mia Casa, an Italian restaurant; Troy, an American-Latin-Syrian mashup; and Quattro, another Italian restaurant.</p>
<p>Like in Damascus and Aleppo, many houses in the Old City of Homs have been renovated and transformed into restaurants specializing in Levantine cuisine. Most notable of these is Beit al-Agha restaurant, situated in a renovated palace that dates back to the mid-19th century with <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_architecture" title="Ottoman architecture">Ottoman</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mamluk_architecture" title="Mamluk architecture">Mamluk</a> architecture,<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> and Julia Dumna Restaurant, which has been described as the best example of traditional Homsi houses, with its white and black stones.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Museums">Museums</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Homs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Museums">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>There are two main museums in Homs, both located in the central part of the city. Azze Hrawe Palace, a former <a href="/wiki/Mamluk" title="Mamluk">Mamluk</a>-era palace belonging to Ali ibn Abi al-Fadl al-Azzhari, a subordinate of <a href="/wiki/Baibars" title="Baibars">Baibars</a>, the Mamluk sultan, is now the National Folklore Museum.<sup id="cite_ref-cart158_69-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cart158-69">[69]</a></sup> Outside the building is a courtyard, occupied on one side by a large terraced <i><a href="/wiki/Liwan" title="Liwan">liwan</a></i> with a conch shell semi-dome. In the opposite wall, there is a carving of two lions, a symbol of Baibars. The first museum built in the city is located along Shoukri al-Quwatly Street and contains a selection of artifacts from the Homs region, covering the time between the prehistoric and Islamic eras.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Festivals">Festivals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Homs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Festivals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Homs has several festivals, and the city annually co-hosts the Desert Folk Festival and the Al-Badiya Festival with <a href="/wiki/Palmyra" title="Palmyra">Palmyra</a>. The Desert Folk Festival is an annual festival of the ancient traditions and costumes of the <i>Badiya</i> (<a href="/wiki/Syrian_Desert" title="Syrian Desert">Syrian Desert</a>) and it includes exhibitions and concerts between Homs and Palmyra. The festival is held in the first week of May.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> The Al-Badiya Festival, which is held mainly in Palmyra with some events in Homs, draws approximately 60,000 tourists during the last week of May. Activities include horse, camel and car races, horse contests, music and theatre shows, antique exhibitions and a crafts market.<sup id="cite_ref-DFF_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DFF-80">[80]</a></sup> Other festivals include the al-Nasarah Festival and the Festival of Krak des Chevaliers and the Valley. An annual festival is held at the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Saint_Elian" title="Church of Saint Elian">Church of Saint Elian</a>, attracting large numbers of pilgrims.<sup id="cite_ref-Beattie.2C_2001.2C_p.208_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Beattie.2C_2001.2C_p.208-81">[81]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Homs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:AL_Karama_stadium.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/AL_Karama_stadium.jpg/220px-AL_Karama_stadium.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/AL_Karama_stadium.jpg/330px-AL_Karama_stadium.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/AL_Karama_stadium.jpg/440px-AL_Karama_stadium.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="600" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:AL_Karama_stadium.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Khaled_Ibn_Al_Walid_Stadium" class="mw-redirect" title="Khaled Ibn Al Walid Stadium">Khaled Ibn Al Walid Stadium</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Homs is home to two <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> clubs. The <a href="/wiki/Al-Karamah_SC" title="Al-Karamah SC">Al-Karamah</a> Sports Club was founded in 1928 and is one of the oldest sports clubs in Syria.<sup id="cite_ref-welt_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-welt-82">[82]</a></sup> Al-Karamah is widely acclaimed on the regional and national levels,<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> having won eight <a href="/wiki/Syrian_League" class="mw-redirect" title="Syrian League">Syrian League</a> titles, and eight <a href="/wiki/Syrian_Cup" title="Syrian Cup">Syrian Cup</a> titles. Al-Karamah was a runner-up in the <a href="/wiki/2006_AFC_Champions_League" title="2006 AFC Champions League">2006 AFC Champions League</a>. The second sports club of the city is <a href="/wiki/Al-Wathba" class="mw-redirect" title="Al-Wathba">Al-Wathba</a> Sports Club, which was founded in 1937. The <a href="/wiki/Khaled_Ibn_Al_Walid_Stadium" class="mw-redirect" title="Khaled Ibn Al Walid Stadium">Khaled Ibn Al Walid Stadium</a> has a 35,000-person capacity and is home to both football clubs.<sup id="cite_ref-welt_82-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-welt-82">[82]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> Homs has produced a number of well-known sportsmen, including footballers <a href="/wiki/Firas_Al_Khatib" class="mw-redirect" title="Firas Al Khatib">Firas Al Khatib</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jehad_Al_Hussain" class="mw-redirect" title="Jehad Al Hussain">Jehad Al Hussain</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Homs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Homs is the capital of the <a href="/wiki/Homs_District" title="Homs District">Homs District</a>, and the capital of the <a href="/wiki/Homs_Governorate" title="Homs Governorate">Homs Governorate</a>—the largest governorate in Syria, and houses the seat of its governor, appointed by the president. The city of Homs is governed by a city council and is home to the Executive Office. The latter consists of nine elected members, in addition to the president of the <a href="/wiki/City_council" title="City council">city council</a>. The Office aids the Governor in making management decisions related to the Governorate, while the city council is responsible for decisions specific to the city of Homs. It is headed by a president, Nadia Kseibi, and is responsible for the day-to-day management of the city.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup></p>
<p>The council's organizational structure is composed of the top leadership, consisting of the president, vice president, and secretary, and the lower leadership, made up of the directors of seventeen city branches: Administrative Affairs, Finance, Technical Affairs, Health Affairs, Legal Affairs, the Fire Department, Mechanisms, Parks, Hygiene, Property, Provisional Register, Services and Maintenance, Works, IT, Planning and Statistics, Culture, and Internal Oversight Service.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Homs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Faculty_of_Medicine_in_Albaath_University,_Syria.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Faculty_of_Medicine_in_Albaath_University%2C_Syria.jpg/220px-Faculty_of_Medicine_in_Albaath_University%2C_Syria.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Faculty_of_Medicine_in_Albaath_University%2C_Syria.jpg/330px-Faculty_of_Medicine_in_Albaath_University%2C_Syria.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Faculty_of_Medicine_in_Albaath_University%2C_Syria.jpg/440px-Faculty_of_Medicine_in_Albaath_University%2C_Syria.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Faculty_of_Medicine_in_Albaath_University,_Syria.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Faculty of Medicine in <a href="/wiki/Al-Baath_University" title="Al-Baath University">Al-Baath University</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Homs is home to the <a href="/wiki/Al-Baath_University" title="Al-Baath University">Al-Baath University</a>, one of four major universities in Syria was founded in 1979. A specialist engineering foundation, the university has one of the largest student bodies.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> It houses several faculties including medicine, engineering, liberal arts, and sciences and a number of two-year career (vocational) institutions. It is the only university in the country to have departments in petroleum engineering and veterinary medicine.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Wadi_International_University" title="Wadi International University">German University</a> at Wadi al-Nasarah opened in 2004 and is located 30 kilometers (19&#160;mi) west of the city. In 2005, the <a href="/wiki/International_School_of_Choueifat" title="International School of Choueifat">International School of Choueifat</a> opened a school outside the city.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Al-Andalus_University_for_Medical_Sciences" title="Al-Andalus University for Medical Sciences">Al-Andalus University for Medical Sciences</a> was established in 2005 near Homs, and is constructing one of its <a href="/wiki/University_Hospital" class="mw-redirect" title="University Hospital">University Hospitals</a> in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup></p>
<p>There are 1,727 schools and 15,000 kindergartens in the Homs Governorate, most of which are public facilities. In 2007, 375,000 students in the governorate were enrolled in elementary schools (6–15 years), 36,000 in high schools (15–18 years), and around 12,000 in vocational training schools.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Local_infrastructure">Local infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Homs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Local infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Homs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Al-Shuhadaa_Square_-_Hims,_Syria.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Al-Shuhadaa_Square_-_Hims%2C_Syria.jpg/220px-Al-Shuhadaa_Square_-_Hims%2C_Syria.jpg" width="220" height="131" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Al-Shuhadaa_Square_-_Hims%2C_Syria.jpg/330px-Al-Shuhadaa_Square_-_Hims%2C_Syria.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Al-Shuhadaa_Square_-_Hims%2C_Syria.jpg/440px-Al-Shuhadaa_Square_-_Hims%2C_Syria.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1022" data-file-height="609" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Al-Shuhadaa_Square_-_Hims,_Syria.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Old Clock Square</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Homs is considered a <a href="/wiki/Transportation_hub" class="mw-redirect" title="Transportation hub">transportation hub</a> in Syria, by virtue of its central location between the coastal cities and the interior.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> The main bus terminal is Karnak, situated along Hama Street, 1.5 kilometers (0.93&#160;mi) north of the city centre on the outskirts. The terminal offers connections to most Syrian cities and <a href="/wiki/Beirut" title="Beirut">Beirut</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">Lebanon</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Carter2_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carter2-93">[93]</a></sup> It also has international bus connections to Lebanon, <a href="/wiki/Jordan" title="Jordan">Jordan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>. A second "luxury" bus station is located a little further north. <a href="/wiki/Minibus" title="Minibus">Minibuses</a> operate from Karnak station with destinations to <a href="/wiki/Tartus" title="Tartus">Tartus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Palmyra" title="Palmyra">Palmyra</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hama" title="Hama">Hama</a> in northern Syria, as well as <a href="/wiki/Baalbek" title="Baalbek">Baalbek</a>, Tripoli, and <a href="/wiki/Beirut" title="Beirut">Beirut</a> in Lebanon. Newer <a href="/wiki/Microbus" class="mw-redirect" title="Microbus">microbuses</a> that mostly travel to Hama are also based in Karnak and are mostly used for quick transportation.</p>
<p>Homs has a large <a href="/wiki/Railway" class="mw-redirect" title="Railway">railway</a> station, with two <a href="/wiki/Chemins_de_Fer_Syriens" class="mw-redirect" title="Chemins de Fer Syriens">Chemins de Fer Syriens</a> operated daily departures to Damascus and Aleppo.<sup id="cite_ref-Carter2_93-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carter2-93">[93]</a></sup> The nearest airports are <a href="/wiki/Bassel_Al-Assad_International_Airport" title="Bassel Al-Assad International Airport">Bassel Al-Assad International Airport</a> in <a href="/wiki/Latakia" title="Latakia">Latakia</a> to the west, <a href="/wiki/Damascus_International_Airport" title="Damascus International Airport">Damascus International Airport</a> to the south, <a href="/wiki/Aleppo_International_Airport" title="Aleppo International Airport">Aleppo International Airport</a> to the north, and <a href="/wiki/Palmyra_Airport" title="Palmyra Airport">Palmyra Airport</a> in the Syrian Desert to the east.</p>
<p>Hama Street starts at the Old Clock Square in the city center and crosses Homs from south to north, where it continues along the neighborhood of al-Khaldiyah on to the Karnak station, and turns into the Homs-Hama-Aleppo highway. <a href="/wiki/Quwatli_Street" class="mw-redirect" title="Quwatli Street">Quwatli Street</a>, named after former president <a href="/wiki/Shukri_al-Quwatli" title="Shukri al-Quwatli">Shukri al-Quwatli</a>, is a short but vital street that connects the Old Clock Square and Quwatli Square in Downtown Homs. It branches into several smaller streets on its western end, one of which is al-Dablan Street which is the main commercial block in the city, and the other continues west to connect with the Homs-<a href="/wiki/Tripoli,_Lebanon" title="Tripoli, Lebanon">Tripoli</a> highway. On the eastern end, al-Quwatli street continues as al-Hamidiyah Street which crosses the old Christian quarter and continues to the eastern edge of the city. The Homs-Damascus highway crosses the city from the south and reaches the city center in Quwatli Square.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Landmarks">Landmarks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Homs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Landmarks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_New_Clock.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/The_New_Clock.jpg/220px-The_New_Clock.jpg" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/The_New_Clock.jpg/330px-The_New_Clock.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/The_New_Clock.jpg/440px-The_New_Clock.jpg 2x" data-file-width="450" data-file-height="600" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_New_Clock.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The New Clock Tower in Homs</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The city itself is famous its historic <a href="/wiki/Mosque" title="Mosque">mosques</a> and <a href="/wiki/Church_(building)" title="Church (building)">churches</a>. It is also well recognized by its twin clock towers. The older one, facing al-Hamidiya Street, was built by the <a href="/wiki/French_mandate_of_Syria" class="mw-redirect" title="French mandate of Syria">French</a> in the early 1930s, and the newer one in al-Quwatli Square facing al-Dablan street. Homs is well known for its historical roofed <i><a href="/wiki/Souk" class="mw-redirect" title="Souk">souks</a></i>. These consist of a complex maze of narrow streets and covered commercial alleys extending from the south and east from the Great Mosque towards the ancient citadel. The <i>souks</i>—lined with grocery and clothing stores, and workshops for carpenters, artisans, cobblers, metalworkers and knife-sharpeners—are busiest in the evening.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup></p>
<p>Homs and the surrounding countryside bear many landmarks, including a <a href="/wiki/World_heritage_site" class="mw-redirect" title="World heritage site">world heritage site</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Krak_des_Chevaliers" title="Krak des Chevaliers">Krak des Chevaliers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Citadel_of_Salah_Ed-Din" title="Citadel of Salah Ed-Din">Citadel of Salah Ed-Din</a>. Other landmarks include the <a href="/wiki/Great_Mosque_of_al-Nuri_(Homs)" title="Great Mosque of al-Nuri (Homs)">Great Mosque of al-Nuri</a>. Originally a pagan temple dedicated to El-Gabal, it was consecrated as the Church of Saint John the Baptist under the Byzantines. Later, it was established as a Friday mosque during the Islamic Arab rule of Homs.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Khalid_ibn_al-Walid_Mosque" title="Khalid ibn al-Walid Mosque">Khalid ibn al-Walid Mosque</a> has been considered "the only edifice of any real note" in Homs, and was built in the last few years of Ottoman rule in Syria during the 1900s. The mosque is named after early Arab general Khalid ibn al-Walid, whose tomb is located within the building.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Um_al-Zennar_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="Um al-Zennar Church">Um al-Zennar Church</a> ("Church of the Virgin's Girdle") was built in 1852 atop an earlier church dating back to the 4th century, and perhaps 59 CE. The other prominent church in Homs is the 5th-century <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Saint_Elian" title="Church of Saint Elian">Church of Saint Elian</a>, built in honor of <a href="/wiki/Christian" title="Christian">Christian</a> martyr Saint Elian, whose tomb is located in the <a href="/wiki/Crypt" title="Crypt">crypt</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Beattie.2C_2001.2C_p.208_81-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Beattie.2C_2001.2C_p.208-81">[81]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Citadel of Homs is situated on one of the largest urban <a href="/wiki/Tell" class="mw-redirect" title="Tell">tells</a> of Syria. It has been archaeologically neglected because of military occupation until recent years. The tell dates back at least to the <a href="/wiki/Early_Bronze_Age" class="mw-redirect" title="Early Bronze Age">Early Bronze Age</a>. The extant Islamic-style walls were built during the Ayyubid period and the Mamluk sultan <a href="/wiki/Baybars" class="mw-redirect" title="Baybars">Baybars</a> subsequently carried out restorations. All of this work is testified by inscriptions although without exception, they are lost. In 1994, a joint Syrian-British team studied the Citadel of Homs, recording the remains of the walls and towers.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Twin_towns_.E2.80.93_Sister_cities">Twin towns – Sister cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Homs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Twin towns – Sister cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil"><img alt="Brazil" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/05/Flag_of_Brazil.svg/22px-Flag_of_Brazil.svg.png" width="22" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/05/Flag_of_Brazil.svg/33px-Flag_of_Brazil.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/05/Flag_of_Brazil.svg/43px-Flag_of_Brazil.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="720" data-file-height="504" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Belo_Horizonte" title="Belo Horizonte">Belo Horizonte</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a> (2001)<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey"><img alt="Turkey" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Flag_of_Turkey.svg/23px-Flag_of_Turkey.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Flag_of_Turkey.svg/35px-Flag_of_Turkey.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Flag_of_Turkey.svg/45px-Flag_of_Turkey.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="800" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Kayseri" title="Kayseri">Kayseri</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a><sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran"><img alt="Iran" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Flag_of_Iran.svg/23px-Flag_of_Iran.svg.png" width="23" height="13" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Flag_of_Iran.svg/35px-Flag_of_Iran.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Flag_of_Iran.svg/46px-Flag_of_Iran.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="630" data-file-height="360" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Yazd" title="Yazd">Yazd</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a><sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
